Free Talk

A Bit of Gossip

[The Story of the Eastern Wing and General Black Horse

— Zhan Lu

After reading my Zhang Sheng Cries, which I wrote the other day, it sparked a discussion among my friends:

Your talk about Zhang Sheng crying in The Story of the Eastern Wing is quite amusing.

I don't see it that way. I'm just riffing on The Journey to the West, and riffing on The Story of the Eastern Wing.

The main character in The Story of the Western Wing is Zhang Sheng; the main character in The Story of the Eastern Wing is also Zhang Sheng. That's quite a coincidence. Zhang Sheng's close friend in The Story of the Western Wing is General White Horse; Zhang Sheng's close friend in The Story of the Eastern Wing is General Black Horse. This is another wonderful parallel. Why didn't you mention it?

True, true. Both General White Horse and General Black Horse are Zhang Sheng's close friends, both upright men who stand tall, and they can certainly be compared. However, General White Horse rescues Zhang Sheng, while General Black Horse awaits rescue from Zhang Sheng. General White Horse rescued Zhang Sheng, saving him from danger; General Black Horse awaits rescue from Zhang Sheng, but Zhang Sheng is unable to save General Black Horse from danger. So, General White Horse in The Story of the Western Wing did not let Zhang Sheng down; but Zhang Sheng in The Story of the Eastern Wing has let General Black Horse down a bit. Because there are so many differences, I didn't mention their close friends General White Horse and General Black Horse when I wrote Zhang Sheng Cries.

In your opinion, which is the more difficult situation, General White Horse's or General Black Horse's?

Of course, White Horse's is easier and Black Horse's is more difficult. It's easier to quell Sun Feihu; it's harder to eliminate Dwarf Tiger. However, difficulty reveals ingenuity, and perhaps Dwarf Tiger will fall at the hands of General Black Horse. Let's wait and see.

Hitler, the Eccentric Genius of Germany 185

— Ma Juncao

What I want to talk about here is the leader of the German Beer Hall Putsch, a follower of Fascism, the head of the National Socialist Party, and the modern eccentric who has attracted worldwide attention: Adolf Hitler.

In the early winter of 1923, Hitler, with the help of General Erich Ludendorff (Chief of Staff of the German Army during World War I), rashly launched a rebellion in Munich, declaring a revolution. In less than a day, it was put down by the local garrison. Hitler inevitably landed in jail, tasting a year of prison life. At that time, men and women throughout Europe regarded this abortive revolution as a laughing stock. Hitler received only ridicule and scorn. But are temporary successes and failures the most important thing? Look, what is Hitler like today?

The establishment of the National Socialist Party was entirely due to Hitler's personal perseverance. Although it has a long history, it has now become the most powerful political party in Germany. In 1924, the party only had twelve seats in the parliament, but in 1928, it leapt to 107 seats. According to general predictions, this year's general election will likely increase to around 230 seats. The rapid expansion of the National Socialist Party's power is due in part to the outstanding oratory genius and organizational perseverance of its leader, Hitler, and in part to the widespread social unrest in Germany: industrial decline, the burden of reparations, and severe unemployment.

Hitler was born in 1889 in Braunau am Inn, Austria. His father was a railway employee. In his youth, Hitler went to South Africa to participate in the Boer War. At the age of twenty-three, he went to Munich, Germany, and worked as a house painter for several years, without any development. When World War I broke out, he joined the German army and spent four years living in the trenches. After the war, he began his political activities, giving speeches to drinkers in beer halls and cafes, criticizing the government's performance, and expressing his personal political views. He used his oratory genius to attract the attention and excitement of many people.

Hitler has a slender, medium build, a straight nose, high cheekbones, a small mustache, and piercing eyes. His proclaimed policies are to abolish the Treaty of Versailles externally, cancel war reparations, establish a dictatorship internally, and eliminate all potential power of the Jews. His ideal supreme figure is Benito Mussolini. Mussolini's photograph is on his desk. He imitates Mussolini's every move, even imitating Mussolini's salute. He often tells reporters that if Heaven were to give Germany a Mussolini, the Germans would kneel down and worship him.

Hitler recently gave a speech in the suburbs of Berlin: "For the past thirteen years, Germans have been constantly in shackles. In the future, the National Socialist Party will clear out the thirty-odd political parties that cannot have a clear and strong policy, and strive for an opportunity to demonstrate the National Socialist Party's policies and capabilities." Look at how great his ambitions are.

Random Thoughts 186

— Mo Yi

Yesterday, four people dressed in black silk short shirts and trousers, holding account book-like notebooks in their hands, burst into the door with smiling faces, and shouted loudly, without knowing who they were talking to: "This year, Shanghai has been ravaged by the Japanese. So many people died in Zhabei, and the weather is hotter than in previous years, so the plague is severe." Before they finished speaking, they placed the notebooks in front of me. I saw that some people had written one yuan, some two yuan, and even five yuan or ten yuan. I was very surprised. Isn't this a donation? Most of the Shanghai plague hospitals are set up by charitable organizations, and I have never heard of them collecting donations. What is going on? Thinking this, I stared at them with suspicion. One of the short, fat men, noticing my expression, smiled and said: "We also live in this neighborhood. For the peace of the tenants in this neighborhood, we have launched a 'Taiping Gong Jiao' [Taoist ritual for peace]. You can write down however much money you want." After hearing his words, I understood their intention and firmly refused: "I won't donate. Not even a penny. Don't say I don't have money, even if I do, I'm not willing to be the son of monks and Taoists. To pay them a sum of money is like letting them create a ruckus that is as scary as hell and scam away a year's worth of food, clothing, and housing. In fact, many people who spend money on rituals often die from the plague. I really don't see what benefits there are to creating these parasites for society. It would be much more meaningful and beneficial to send the money to the Northeast to buy bullets for the volunteers to kill our enemies."

XXXXXXXXX

Recently, my wife has been frequently ill. She was introduced by Mrs. Lin, who believes in taking medicine even when healthy, to famous doctors in Shanghai for treatment. According to her experience, this doctor can indeed work wonders and cure diseases with his medicine. So I accompanied my wife to the doctor's office. We registered for the price of 4.40 yuan. Because we arrived late, our number was 156. We waited from 11:00 AM until 3:00 PM in the afternoon before it was my wife's turn. I watched the doctor examine my wife and was shocked. He put his fingers on my wife's pulse while looking at a stack of other people's prescriptions and reporting the names of the medicine in his mouth. The examination was over in less than five minutes, and someone else filled in the prescription. Another half hour passed before we got the prescription. After returning home, I tore up the prescription and forbade my wife to take his medicine. My reasoning was: it's better to let nature take its course than to become a wronged ghost. Perhaps she won't die; otherwise, you can't be sure.

XXXXXXXXX

One day, I went to visit a wealthy man about a friend's business. While I was waiting for the wealthy man, who was smoking opium upstairs, in his luxurious living room, I caught a glimpse of a servant in the courtyard feeding two large foreign dogs with two large basins of fragrant beef. I became impatient waiting, so I walked into the courtyard to watch the dogs eat beef. I unintentionally asked the servant how much beef these two dogs ate every day. He replied: "At least three yuan worth of beef and 40 cents worth of milk every day." I was stunned. This is truly a wealthy man's extravagance. Just for two dogs, he spends more than one hundred yuan a month. How much better it would be to use that money to help the disaster victims. In my mind's eye, I seemed to see a large group of disaster victims scrambling to eat rotten human flesh.

A New Chemical Industry Worth Introducing 187

— Pi Man

The dye indigo used for dyeing is made from substances extracted from coal tar oil. Therefore, it is called coal tar oil dye, also known as aniline dye. Aniline is extracted from the coal tar oil, benzol, which is treated with nitric acid, initially transforming into nitrobenzene, and then reduced by light gasification, thus becoming aniline. This is the basic raw material for manufacturing the dye indigo. The term aniline dye is derived from this.

Recently, new leaders in the local dye industry, Li Shuyan, Wang Zuolin, Wu Xingzai, and others, have united with various sectors to launch the Zhongfu Chemical Manufacturing Factory Co., Ltd. with a capital of 1 million yuan. The various initiators have committed to contributing more than 400,000 yuan. The company specializes in the manufacture of the dye indigo. Indigo is made from camphor and acetic acid, etc., extracted from coal tar oil. This is the latest manufacturing method. The company held an inaugural meeting, and publicly elected Qiu Pengnian as the chairman of the fundraising committee. Xu Xinliu, Zou Bingwen, Dong Rongqing, and others were elected as preparation committee members. Dong Rongqing was elected as the director of the preparatory office, with Li Shuyan as his deputy. The registration is currently in progress. Fundraising is expected to begin soon. Mr. Dong graduated from the Chemistry Department of the Pratt Institute of Technology in the United States. He has conducted on-site inspections of major European and American dye factories, and interned at the BASF factory (I.G. Farben) in Germany. He has served as a managing director of the Hangzhou Wulin Paper Mill, a technician at the Shanghai Zhongyi Chemical Factory, and is a member of the Chinese Engineering Society, the Science Society of China, and the American Chemical Society. He has a wealth of experience in practical chemical work. He is also shrewd, capable, and amiable. Many people from all walks of life are supporting him.

The annual value of dye imports into China is more than 100 million yuan. It is a huge outflow of wealth that should be curbed as soon as possible. Moreover, dye factories are closely related to national defense, as they provide chemical warfare weapons. With the daily increase of foreign aggression, it is especially urgent to set them up. This kind of enterprise can not only generate profit, but also defend the country against enemies. When fundraising begins, Chinese citizens will surely invest enthusiastically. It can be predicted. (The company's preparatory office is located at No. 14 Guangdong Road) A pioneering move worthy of my introduction.

Looking at the Studio, Boasting About the Muscles: Kang Youwei and Liang Qichao (Middle) 188

— Gan Yi

Qichao, styled Zhuoru, also styled Rengong, was a native of Xinhui, Guangdong. When Youwei lectured at Wanmu Thatched Cottage, Qichao was the most knowledgeable and eloquent. None of the disciples could match him. Youwei compared himself to Confucius and likened Qichao to Yan Yuan, hence his fame. When Li Ruifen presided over the Guangdong provincial examination, he saw Qichao's writing, like the Yangtze River pouring down thousands of miles, and did not dismiss it for its superficiality or brevity, placing it at the top. He looked around and said, "This man's fame and position will surpass mine in the future." He summoned him for an interview and was even more amazed by his talent. Knowing that he was not yet married, he gave his younger sister in marriage. When Ruifen returned to the capital, he praised Qichao greatly among officials and scholars. Everyone in the capital knew of Liang, the recommended scholar, and competed to see him. Qichao had a close friendship with Tan Sitong. Sitong recommended him to Chen Baozhen, the governor of Hunan, and he was put in charge of the Changsha School of Current Affairs. Although he criticized and rejected the Manchus, he advocated reform. Elders such as Wang Yunxuan and Wang Xianqian were shocked to hear this, saying that Qichao's inflammatory words were disrupting politics. However, Baozhen was unmoved, as Baozhen had always sympathized with Kang and Liang. His son, Sanwei, once argued that a strong country must undergo reform. Xu Renduo, the education commissioner, was also a reformer. After befriending Qichao, they often discussed national affairs until late at night. He secretly wrote to his father, Zhijing, stating that Qichao's talent was sufficient for great responsibility and requested that he be recommended to the court. Zhijing was then a vice minister of the Ministry of Rites. One day, Emperor Dezong summoned him and asked about talented people for the new policies. Zhijing recommended Qichao. He received an imperial decree granting him the rank of sixth grade and assigning him to the Translation Bureau of the Printing Office. He was about to be put to great use when the political upheaval occurred. Qichao had already gone to Shanghai for the Current Affairs Newspaper and avoided the disaster. He quickly went to Japan and wrote "A Record of the Hundred Days Reform," criticizing Empress Dowager Cixi and lamenting that Emperor Dezong could not fulfill his ambitions. From then on, he lived in Japan for a long time, editing and publishing the "Qingyi Bao" (Public Opinion Journal) and "Xinmin Congbao" (New Citizen Journal). Because of his fluent writing, almost everyone had a copy. At the end of the Xuantong era, Zheng Xiaoxu, Zhang Sai, Tang Shouqian, and others established the Preparatory Constitutionalism Association, communicating with Qichao. Qichao published the "Guofeng Bao" (National Customs Journal), criticizing relatives of the imperial family for manipulating power and interfering in politics. He also opposed the Tongmenghui. At that time, Zhang Binglin was writing the "Minbao" (People's Journal), and their views differed. He often wrote abusive articles. Qichao did not back down and responded with harsh words. Everyone knew that Qichao liked to argue. After Yuan Shikai entered Beijing from Huan Shang, he intended to seize power. He sent Tang Shaoyi and Yang Shiqi south to negotiate peace and summoned Qichao back. Qichao, who had been dormant for a long time, thought about taking action. Knowing that Yuan Shikai was superior in strategy, he hurriedly set out. From Korea, he passed through Shenyang. Xiong Xiling, the salt transport commissioner of the three eastern provinces, welcomed him outside the city. During their meeting, Qichao said, "Political corruption is based on the blind and reckless actions of the nobility, without the participation of the Han people. We were once loyal to the Emperor and supported the monarchy. Although Emperor Dezong is no longer alive and the young Emperor is ignorant, the regent is dim-witted. The responsibility of those who die later is even greater. Now, many people advocate democracy and republicanism, which is not suitable for the national condition. Even if we talk about republicanism, we should have a constitutional monarchy." Xiling agreed with his words, which were reported to Yuan Shikai. He requested an imperial decree appointing Qichao as the Vice Minister of the Ministry of Justice, urging him to take office quickly. Qichao hesitated and did not go. Yuan Shikai sent his trusted aide to urge him again, and then he left.

Commercial News

Gold Price Falls Six Taels and Two Mace 189

The market is mediocre and trending downward. Yesterday, the gold standard market was mediocre but continued to decline. The daily ups and downs only amounted to one or two taels, and the total was only four taels. The cash transactions of various brokers were complex and idle. Finally, it fell more than six taels. It opened below the 720 tael mark. Although the silver market rebounded, it was unmoved. Initially, it was influenced by the opposite rise in U.S. silver futures and private telegrams. Sharp Rise in Silk and Tea Prices in Hangzhou 203

Recently, the raw silk market in foreign firms has become increasingly active. The price of factory-dried silk has risen by dozens of taels. The price of domestic silk has also risen sharply. Various silk weaving factories are purchasing domestic silk due to the high price of factory-dried silk. The price of fine and fat silk in Hangzhou has risen sharply by eight or nine yuan per hundred taels. Fine silk is now priced at thirty-four yuan, and fat silk at twenty-six yuan. In the local silk market, manufacturers are aware of the strong demand for yellow and white factory-dried silk from Europe and the United States, coupled with the speculative hoarding by merchants, and the scarce stock of raw materials (i.e., dried cocoons) cannot meet the demand, so they insist on selling at high prices. Yesterday, many telegrams were sent out for factory-dried silk. The factory price for Grade B white factory-dried silk is seven hundred fifty-six taels, and even the price for Sichuan-Shandong yellow factory-dried silk is six hundred forty-five taels. A decision must be made after the telegram is forwarded. Yesterday, the market sentiment was held back, and both Chinese and foreign parties were waiting to see how the overseas telegram would be forwarded before making a decision. Transactions are pending.

Unexpected Arrival of Galvanized Iron from Tianjin in the Hardware Market 205

Hardware transactions have been quiet recently, presumably due to the poor environment, and there is little development in various sectors, so the number of goods opened throughout the city is still limited. Although bamboo steel, lead, tinplate, British steel plate, and new lead wire were sold yesterday, there has been little change in prices. However, there is a surprising piece of news, that is, it is rumored in the market that a Tianjin company has shipped six- or seven-foot flat galvanized iron to Shanghai. In the past, the Tianjin companies and other neighboring companies in Beiping, Qingdao, and Jinan all purchased flat galvanized iron from Shanghai. In the past four or five years, due to the arrival of galvanized iron from Japan, the market in the northern ports has been strongly occupied. Therefore, the flat galvanized iron in Shanghai could not be shipped to Tianjin and other places. Now, there is a turning point in the Shanghai galvanized iron market, and Tianjin suddenly has spot goods that can be shipped and sold in Shanghai. This has surprised all hardware merchants. However, the reporter could not prejudge whether the goods are from Japan or England because he has not seen them personally.

Supplement to the Shanghai News

Speech

County Magistrate Punished with Kneeling and Military Beating 210

— Fo

The county magistrate is the official closest to the people, and therefore the quality of the county magistrate is of utmost importance to the people. Strict supervision by both the government and the people is necessary. According to a telegram from Jinan yesterday, Han Fuju interrogated Zou County Magistrate Xue Dayu in the Provincial

Government for abusing fines. Xue was sentenced to kneel, dismissed from his post, and fined 1,500 yuan to compensate the people for their losses. Lu Juemin, the county magistrate of Pingyuan, was accused of abusing fines during his tenure in Changshan. He was sentenced to kneel, receive fifty blows, and fined 1,500 yuan to compensate the people for their losses. Such things, if heard occasionally, would surely be considered strange news, seemingly an extremely outrageous act. However, I want to consider this carefully. The embezzlement and perversion of justice by county magistrates in various places can be considered a very common epidemic. Although the government has promulgated the regulations for the punishment of officials for a long time, and there is a Supervisory Yuan to impeach them, corrupt and lawless officials still operate everywhere. There are three reasons for this. First, many current county magistrates have powerful backers. These county magistrates rely on their support and act recklessly, disregarding national laws. Second, the people fear officials as they fear gods. Even if they suffer injustice to any extent, they dare not appeal to higher authorities, fearing that officials will protect each other, and if the lawsuit is unsuccessful, it will be even more disastrous. Third, although the government has regulations for the punishment of officials and a Supervisory Yuan, there is no effective method of supervision. Even if officials are extorting the people and imposing harsh taxes every day, how can the government know? Therefore, laws are treated as trivial matters and are completely disregarded.

If such county magistrates are not punished like Han Fuju's kneeling and military beating, there is no other way. In the Republican era, the ritual of kneeling has long been abolished, and punishing by kneeling seems inappropriate. Furthermore, the punishment of military beating is used for soldiers, and using it on county magistrates this time naturally seems inappropriate. The saying goes, "Use severe punishments to govern a chaotic country." The methods of punishment in past dynasties, whether severe or lenient, were not fixed. As long as the offenders are afraid, that is enough. The so-called "killing a dog to scare the monkeys." Although this saying does not conform to modern trends, it is very suitable for officials who are greedy and insatiable. Only such methods may be effective for such county magistrates. Therefore, I only feel relieved about Han's beating of the county magistrate. Originally, princes and commoners are equal before the law. What does it matter to beat such county magistrates a few times?

However, this method can only bring temporary satisfaction and is not a fundamental solution. The fundamental solution, on the government's side, although there is a Supervisory Yuan, it is still necessary to study how to supervise and how to observe. If we only rely on people's accusations and send people to investigate, what if the people dare not report? What if the investigators have problems? The injustice will inevitably sink to the bottom of the sea. Therefore, the best method is to let the people supervise, which is closer and more intimate. The people's suffering should be addressed by the people themselves. But now, the people do not pay attention to such events, which is truly strange.

Literature and Art

Inscription for Zhang Zijin's Painting 211

— Xiaochang

Your home is by the Melon Islet, with two or three thatched cottages. Willows rustle before the door, and water flows gently beyond the railing. What can be seen far and wide? Only the mountains of Jiangnan. The mountain air is good every day, and your heart is at ease every day. Put it into painting, hang it on the wall and look at it. A clear breeze comes to the seat, bringing a slight chill in June.

Feeling Autumn 212

— Zhu Songling

The falling leaves of the wutong tree startle, and warriors already grieve for autumn. Moreover, with continuous rain, how can the courtyard be filled with sorrow? The sound of insects chirps from all sides, and the flames of fireflies flash in the high building. The north of the mountain pass is not seen, and the wind and clouds darken the Dipper.

Science

Glass 213

— Yin Zhen

We see glass everywhere. It is a transparent solid, resistant to water and acids. Because of its valuable properties, it has a wide range of uses, including optical instruments and all kinds of daily necessities and decorations.

Glass can be divided into three types: 1. Ordinary glass (soda glass), 2. Hard glass (potash glass), and 3. Aluminum glass.

The components of glass generally include ash, potassium carbonate, and ordinary silicon dioxide.

However, the components vary depending on the type of glass.

1. Ordinary glass is composed of sodium silicate, calcium silicate, and silicon dioxide.

2. Hard glass has the same components.

3. Aluminum glass is composed of potassium silicate and aluminum silicate.

The properties of glass also vary depending on the type.

1. Ordinary glass has a slightly greenish color, is easily melted, and has weak resistance to chemicals.

2. Hard glass is colorless, difficult to melt, and has strong resistance to chemicals.

3. Aluminum glass is very soft, easily melted, heavy, and has a strong refractive index.

The uses of glass are determined by its properties. 1. Ordinary glass is used to make window panes, bottles, and ordinary utensils.

2. Hard glass is used to make decorations and chemical instruments. 3. Aluminum glass is used to make decorations and optical instruments. The raw materials for glass are 1. Ordinary glass: sodium carbonate or sodium silicate and charcoal silicon dioxide (silica) (sand or quartz) calcium carbonate.

2. Hard glass: potassium carbonate silicon dioxide, calcium carbonate.

3. Aluminum glass: potassium carbonate, silicon dioxide, aluminum dioxide.

The manufacturing method of glass is to melt all the raw materials together. When it is melted into a liquid, cool it slightly and blow it into a mold to form various utensils.

The method of making colored glass is the same as ordinary glass, but adding a small amount of metal gas compounds will produce color. Aluminum (Co) becomes blue, chromium (Cr) becomes green, gold (Au) becomes red, and uranium becomes yellow.

To make opaque milky white glass, add feldspar or fluorite.

School Photo

Miss L 214

— Shi

Page 20

Miss L is a thorough modern student. Every day when she goes to school, in addition to a few textbooks, she also has a love novel and a wallet. This wallet is like a cosmetics store in Jinli, where all kinds of cosmetics can be found.

It has been less than two weeks since the summer school started, and no one among the students does not know her name, because Miss L is not only a modern student, but also a socialite.

Although Miss L does not have natural beauty, she has the beauty of material and makeup, which is enough to intoxicate the heroes. So now she has become a plaything for some of the male students and is used by them.

One morning, after the first class, Miss L pulled Ms. W out of the classroom to talk. She said: "Mr. C is an excellent student at XX Middle School. He has admired you for a long time. You shouldn't be so cruel. I know this is a woman's way, and I can't just blame you. But you must know that Mr. C is going to seek death because of your cold attitude. He said that he wanted to sacrifice for love. Sister W, think about it yourself. Someone is going to die for you!" These words were nothing else, but Ms. W was so frightened that she broke into a cold sweat. Indeed, such words containing seduction and intimidation are so terrible for a woman who has not experienced the baptism of love!

A day later, Miss L sent a pink love letter to Ms. W on behalf of Mr. C. Miss L, who uses the name of studying to be a socialite, is very used to this kind of love letter, but Ms. W is an orphan without parents or siblings. Her coming to school is to build a foundation for her future independence. However, she is also an emotional person. This kind of love letter is very difficult for Ms. W.

Now Ms. W has been led astray by Miss L. The two different paths in front of her will bring Ms. W future happiness and depression. If Ms. W does not wake up early, I am afraid that she will be assimilated by Miss L soon.

Society Reform Discussion

My Opinion on the Trend of Improving Men's and Women's Clothing Towards Simplicity 215

— Siwei

Many people have discussed the issue of improving men's and women's clothing. I will not be too verbose and will offer a few more words. I can divide the current social situation into three classes below.

A. Aristocracy

B. Well-off

C. Commoners

[A] Aristocratic families do not know the difficulty and origin of material resources. When the lights are lit up, we can see the extravagant aristocratic young masters and ladies wearing brightly colored imported clothes and riding fast cars to show off their wealth. It may not be important for them to spend a few more dollars and change their clothes every day, but it may arouse the covetousness of petty thieves. As the saying goes, "Extravagant possessions invite theft, and alluring looks invite licentiousness!"

[B] Well-off families may have a psychology of currying favor with the powerful and have to put on a show. Therefore, their clothes are almost the same as the aristocratic class. As the saying goes, "A donkey running after a horse." I wonder how they can keep up, and they may even sprain their feet.

[C] The commoner class is very different from the bourgeois class. They all rely on the rewards earned by their own labor to maintain their family's life. For example, ordinary employees in shops or companies earn only dozens of yuan a month. Their clothes can be more simple, but in fact, it is often not the case, especially women. They never pity the money earned by their fathers, brothers, or husbands, and do not think about being frugal. They may even quarrel with their fathers, brothers, or husbands for new clothes. Even if the husband has no money, he must borrow it to buy them. Isn't this what people call "dying to show off"?

In short, the current phenomenon in China cannot be improved merely by a few worn-out pens and a few newspapers publicizing it. It must be done in practice. Moreover, most of the beautiful clothes worn by people of the upper, middle, and lower classes are imported goods. The amount of money flowing out every year is really alarming. Therefore, I am not afraid of the readers' boredom and will write it out as much as possible. One is for frugality, which is a virtue, and can improve customs. The other is for the sake of the survival of the great Chinese nation. I hope that all Chinese people will change to wearing domestic clothes to avoid the outflow of money. You see, foreigners earn the money of the Chinese people and use it to make guns to fight against China. That is our own Chinese people's lack of competitiveness! (Donate rewards to the Northeast Volunteer Army)

Family Problems

The Master of the Irritable Temper 216

— Niaozuo

The "Master of the Irritable Temper" mentioned here is "Mrs. Zhang," who lives with us in the same house. Although she is considered an intellectual, her harshness and irritability towards the maids are so severe that anyone who sees it will have a dizzy spell!

She is one of those who like to read our old Shanghai News every morning, and she loves to read this small corner of the "Local Supplement." Therefore, I am now specifically listing her recent irritable actions and publishing them here. I hope that after she reads it, her face will turn red at that moment, and then she will strive to change her ways and stop doing that kind of unconscious behavior that is criticized as "acting important" and "acting high and mighty."

Below is a true portrayal of her irritable actions.

One day, her maid, called Qin Ma, bought some vegetables and came back to her and said: "Madam! The vegetables have been bought. Please go to the kitchen to take a look." This was her daily routine, fearing that the maids would lie and she had to check the things they bought. Unexpectedly, this time she rolled her eyes and said: "You all have become madams! Do you want me to walk to the kitchen to see the vegetables that you bought?" Qin Ma was scolded for no reason. The next day, she bought some vegetables and immediately brought them to her to see. Unexpectedly, she became angry again and said angrily: "Oh! Are you crazy? Have all those years been transferred to the yellow dog? Filthy things, bring them into the room, do you think I've broken my legs and can't go to the kitchen to see?"

XXXX

The evening glow spread across the sky like a lovely beauty. Qin Ma wondered why her mistress had not yet given the order to prepare dinner. Taking the opportunity, she went to ask her if she needed to prepare dinner. She seemed to see a black lacquered bench beside her, acting coquettishly and even more domineeringly: "Are you hungry like a dog? Why are you urging me so impatiently!" Everyone, think about it: would Qin Ma dare to ask her again next time, only to be rudely dismissed? However, she was also harmed by her trembling liver fire: it turned out that two evenings later, she saw that dinner had not been prepared, and she called Qin Ma to question her: "The electric lights have been turned on for a long time. Is this your first day here? Why hasn't dinner been served yet? You've really become madams, and everything has to be respectfully requested! Such a clumsy thing like an abacus bead!"

XXXX

The motive for writing this article is not only dedicated to her, but also dedicated to all the young masters and madams who have servants. It is also a sorrowful voice on behalf of those servants who, for the sake of poverty, do not hesitate to abandon their flesh and blood and bow their heads to work like cattle and horses, calling for help from the young masters and madams.

The defendant Gu Fusheng shall repay the plaintiff 135 yuan in silver dollars, with 120 yuan accruing interest at a rate of 2% per annum from April 14, 1931, and the remaining 15 yuan accruing interest at a rate of 2% per annum from October 4, 1931, until the day of execution. The plaintiff's remaining claims are rejected. The defendant Gu Fusheng shall bear nine-tenths of the litigation costs, and the plaintiff shall bear one-tenth.
